style="text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/Ada_(programming_language)" title="Ada (programming language)">Ada 95</a>, <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-influenceSharp_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-influenceSharp-4">[4]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/C99" title="C99">C99</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chapel_(programming_language)" title="Chapel (programming language)">Chapel</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-chplspec_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-chplspec-5">[5]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/PHP" title="PHP">PHP</a>, <a href="/wiki/Python_(programming_language)" title="Python (programming language)">Python</a>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></td>/n</tr>/n<tr>/n<td colspan="2" class="hlist" style="text-align:center;border-top: 1px solid #aaa; padding-top: 3px;">/n<ul>/n<li><a href="/wiki/File:Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg/16px-Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg.png" width="16" height="16" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg/24px-Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg/32px-Wikibooks-logo-en-noslogan.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="400" /></a> <a href="https://en.wikibooks.org/wiki/C%2B%2B_Programming" class="extiw" title="wikibooks:C++ Programming">C++ Programming</a> at Wikibooks</li>/n</ul>/n</td>/n</tr>/n</table>/n<p><b>C++</b> (<a href="/wiki/English_alphabet#Letter_names" title="English alphabet">pronounced</a> <i>cee plus plus</i> <span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/iː/: 'ee' in 'fleece'">iː</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">ʌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'p' in 'pie'">p</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span><span title="/ʌ/: 'u' in 'cut'">ʌ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span></span>/</a></span></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/General-purpose_programming_language" title="General-purpose programming language">general-purpose programming language</a>. It has <a href="/wiki/Imperative_programming" title="Imperative programming">imperative</a>, <a href="/wiki/Object-oriented_programming" title="Object-oriented programming">object-oriented</a> and <a href="/wiki/Generic_programming" title="Generic programming">generic</a> programming features, while also providing facilities for <a href="/wiki/Low-level_programming_language" title="Low-level programming language">low-level</a> <a href="/wiki/Memory_(computing)" class="mw-redirect" title="Memory (computing)">memory</a> manipulation.</p>/n<p>It was designed with a bias toward <a href="/wiki/System_programming" title="System programming">system programming</a> and <a href="/wiki/Embedded_software" title="Embedded software">embedded</a>, resource-constrained and large systems, with <a href="/wiki/Performance_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Performance (software)">performance</a>, efficiency and flexibility of use as its design highlights.<sup id="cite_ref-Stroustrup1_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stroustrup1-7">[7]</a></sup> C++ has also been found useful in many other contexts, with key strengths being software infrastructure and resource-constrained applications,<sup id="cite_ref-Stroustrup1_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Stroustrup1-7">[7]</a></sup> including <a href="/wiki/Application_software" title="Application software">desktop applications</a>, servers (e.g. <a href="/wiki/E-commerce" title="E-commerce">e-commerce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" title="Web search engine">web search</a> or <a href="/wiki/SQL" title="SQL">SQL</a> servers), and performance-critical applications (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Telephone_switches" class="mw-redirect" title="Telephone switches">telephone switches</a> or <a href="/wiki/Space_probes" class="mw-redirect" title="Space probes">space probes</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-applications_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-applications-8">[8]</a></sup> C++ is a <a href="/wiki/Compiled_language" title="Compiled language">compiled language</a>, with implementations of it available on many platforms. Many vendors provide <a href="/wiki/List_of_compilers#C.2B.2B_compilers" title="List of compilers">C++ compilers</a>, including the <a href="/wiki/Free_Software_Foundation" title="Free Software Foundation">Free Software Foundation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a>, and <a href="/wiki/IBM" title="IBM">IBM</a>.</p>/n<p>C++ is standardized by the <a href="/wiki/International_Organization_for_Standardization" title="International Organization for Standardization">International Organization for Standardization</a> (ISO), with the latest standard version ratified and published by ISO in December 2014 as <i><a href="#Standardization">ISO/IEC 14882</a>:2014</i> (informally known as <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B14" title="C++14">C++14</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-isocpp2011_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-isocpp2011-9">[9]</a></sup> The C++ programming language was initially standardized in 1998 as <i>ISO/IEC 14882:1998</i>, which was then amended by the <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B03" title="C++03">C++03</a>, <i>ISO/IEC 14882:2003</i>, standard. The current C++14 standard supersedes these and <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B11" title="C++11">C++11</a>, with <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B14" title="C++14">new features</a> and an enlarged <a href="#Standard_library">standard library</a>. Before the initial standardization in 1998, C++ was developed by <a href="/wiki/Bjarne_Stroustrup" title="Bjarne Stroustrup">Bjarne Stroustrup</a> at <a href="/wiki/Bell_Labs" title="Bell Labs">Bell Labs</a> since 1979, as an extension of the <a href="/wiki/C_(programming_language)" title="C (programming language)">C language</a> as he wanted an efficient and flexible language similar to C, which also provided high-level features for program organization. The <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B17" title="C++17">C++17</a> standard is due in July 2017, with the draft largely implemented by some compilers already, and <a href="/wiki/C%2B%2B20" title="C++20">C++20</a> is the next planned standard thereafter.</p>/n<p>Many other programming languages have been influenced by C++, including <a href="/wiki/C_Sharp_(programming_language)" title="C Sharp (programming language)">C#</a>, <a href="/wiki/D_(programming_language)" title="D (programming language)">D</a>, <a href="/wiki/Java_(programming_language)" title="Java (programming language)">Java</a>, and newer versions of C.</p>/n<p></p>/n<div id="toc" class="toc">/n<div class="toctitle">/n<h2>Contents</h2>/n</div>/n<ul>/n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-1"><a href="#History"><span class="toctext">Etymology</span></a></li>/n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-3"><a href="#Philosophy"><span class="tocnumber">1.2</span> <span class="toctext">Philosophy</span></a></li>/n<li
